The Boston-based company joins a half-dozen others, including MGM and longtime daily fantasy sports rival FanDuel, with deals that allow them the rights to official betting data and NBA logos. Professional sports leagues have long banned any connection to gambling. But in the past few years they have embraced it and sought to profit from both daily fantasy sports and outright gambling on games. Last year, the U.S. Supreme Court tossed out a law that in effect prohibited sports gambling in most states. In this new role, Calder\u00f3n will work closely with NBPA Executive Director Michele Roberts and the NBPA\u2019s senior management team to advise on union strategy as well as on specific issues relevant to current NBA players. He will be the first to serve in this role of Special Assistant, a season-long consulting position created by the NBPA specifically for a recent NBA player. The Special Assistant will help bridge the gap between current players and NBPA staff, giving guidance on the issues faced by players currently in the league and focusing on ways the union can better engage with their members. Calder\u00f3n will hold this position for the 2019-2020 NBA season and will maintain the ability to pursue other business opportunities outside of his role with the union. He will work out of the NBPA\u2019s headquarters in Midtown Manhattan and will travel with NBPA senior management to union team meetings throughout the year. At the end of the season, Calder\u00f3n\u2019s term will come to a close and he will assist with the onboarding of a new Special Assistant for the 2020-2021 NBA season. Calder\u00f3n began his NBA career in 2005, signing with the Toronto Raptors after several years of playing professionally in Europe. The Spanish point guard played for the Raptors for seven seasons before being traded to the Detroit Pistons in 2012. After a year with the Pistons, he went on to play for the Dallas Mavericks, New York Knicks, Los Angeles Lakers, Atlanta Hawks and Cleveland Cavaliers before returning to Detroit in 2019. During his 14-year tenure in the NBA, Calder\u00f3n left his mark on and off the court, leading the league in free throw percentage (2008-2009) and three-point shooting percentage (2012-2013) while also working on global initiatives as an ambassador for UNICEF and as the creator of his own foundation. In addition to his NBA career, Calder\u00f3n has also experienced much success on the international level. Representing his home country of Spain, he participated in numerous FIBA EuroBaskets and World Cups as well as the last four Summer Olympic Games, taking home a total of 11 medals over the last 20 years. \u201cIn this new role, Jos\u00e9 will be an invaluable resource for the NBPA,\u201d said NBPA Executive Director Michele Roberts. \u201cComing straight off of his 14th NBA season, Jos\u00e9 brings a unique perspective to our organization through his understanding of the current issues our players are facing. We are eager to have access to his unparalleled wealth of knowledge and experience.\u201d \u201cAfter all these years of playing, this role checked all the boxes of what I was looking for as a transition from my basketball career,\u201d said Calder\u00f3n. \u201cBeing able to work alongside Michele and the other union departments will be a great opportunity to learn and explore the other side of professional basketball. Coming off a Friday night game in which James and Doncic recorded triple-doubles in a thrilling overtime matchup won by the Lakers , the pair did it again in separate games Sunday.  Doncic posted 29 points, 14 rebounds and 15 assists in the Mavericks\u2019 131-111 crushing of the Cavaliers. With Sunday\u2019s performance, Doncic became the first player in NBA history to record at least 29 points, 15 assists and 13 rebounds in back-to-back games. In Friday\u2019s losing effort, he put up 31 points, 13 rebounds and a career-high 15 assists. Doncic, 20, also became the youngest player in NBA history to log consecutive 25-point triple-doubles, per Elias Stats Bureau. Doncic needed the second-fewest number of games in NBA history to record his first streak of 25-point triple-doubles (his 78th career NBA game). Only Oscar Robertson \u2014 who accomplished the feat in five games \u2014 did it sooner. He joins legend Jason Kidd as only the second player in Mavericks history to have back-to-back 15-assist games. For his part, LeBron had 21 points, 13 assists and 11 rebounds to become the first Laker to record back-to-back triple-doubles since Lamar Odom in 2006. Led by LeBron and Anthony Davis, the Lakers got past the Spurs 103-96 . With two steals, LeBron moved up to 15th on the all-time steals list with 1,945. In Friday\u2019s game, the future Hall-of-Famer recorded 39 points, 12 rebounds, 16 assists and four steals. He was the first Laker to clear the 30-10-15 mark since Magic Johnson in 1990. It was James\u2019 82nd career triple-double, and 30th with at least 30 points. Sunday\u2019s triple-double was the 83rd of his career, now in his 17th season."},{"id":30930,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/gregg-popovich-letter-john-carlos-us-olympic-hall-fame","date":"2019-11-03","title":"Gregg Popovich congratulates American sprinter John Carlos before Hall of Fame induction","content":"SAN ANTONIO \u2014 San Antonio Spurs coach Gregg Popovich shared a portion of the contents of a congratulatory note sent recently to American sprinter John Carlos, who will be inducted Friday along with Tommie Smith into the U.S. Olympic and Paralympic Hall of Fame . Carlos and Smith will be inducted into the Hall more than 50 years after raising their fists in protest of racism at the 1968 Olympic games in Mexico City. \u201cI actually used the word \u2018long overdue\u2019,\u201d Popovich said he wrote in the note. \u201cThen I gave him a little bit of crap on the side. But to see it just brought a great smile, not just to my face, but our coaches and the players who were here when he came in and talked to him. He\u2019s a special guy.\u201d Carlos and Smith created one of the most enduring images of the civil rights movement with their silent protest at the 1968 Olympics in Mexico City. The moment resulted in a national firestorm after Smith and Carlos bowed their heads and raised black-gloved fists on the medal stand after they captured first and third, respectively, in the 200-meter final. Carlos visited the Spurs back in 2015 to share his story with the team. \u201cI communicated to Dr. John [Carlos] because he has been kind enough to come in and talk to our team in the past, and we have kept up a pretty good relationship,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cHe\u2019s somebody who has suffered a great deal, and it just seems like it always takes those kinds of acts that he and Tommie Smith participated in to make social activism get to the point where something actually happens because people who are in their comfortable positions \u2014 white people \u2014 don\u2019t really get it.\u201d Carlos\u2019 and Smith\u2019s protest came with harsh repercussions, as the two received death threats and widespread condemnation from the public back home in America. The U.S. track and field team suspended both and sent them home from the Olympics. They were vilified for several years, and experienced homelessness and unemployment as a result of their protest at the Olympics. \u201cIt\u2019s always, \u2018In time, it will come,\u2019 \u201d Popovich added. \u201cAnd they have no feeling for what a person of color experiences on a minute-to-minute basis; not just physically but psychologically, opportunity-wise, all that sort of thing. So, for them to do what they did, knowing full-well, being intelligent people, that it was going to limit their opportunities for the rest of their lives probably, and they did it anyway \u2026 that\u2019s huge. That\u2019s like a Muhammad Ali moment, what they did. Great credit, which isn\u2019t what they were looking for, but kudos for great courage and being able to do that under ridiculously difficult circumstances.\u201d * * * Michael C. They knew, and you knew, and they knew you knew, that the five-year thrill ride had reached the station. Yet the Warriors couldn\u2019t exactly speak truth to power because, well, that\u2019d be kinda-sorta breaking the competition code that says you must ignore the grim warning signs (even when those signs are more in your face than Draymond Green in a bad mood). But now? Today it\u2019s safe for them to come out, shout it out and get it off their chest and conscious. They may even feel better about it. The same basketball gods that have been so kind to Golden State this decade just issued it a punishment and a pass the other night. Stephen Curry\u2019s broken left hand is the excuse the Warriors need to concede that, indeed, this is a Gap Year and it\u2019s time to plan and build around 2020-21. They can officially play that card and nobody will blame them, not even those fans who paid roughly a trust fund for those nice seats at the new Chase Center . Here\u2019s what the Warriors need to do, should do, must do: Preserve Curry and Klay Thompson as much as possible \u2014 even if that means shelving them for the year \u2014 and pour Draymond a glass of wine after every game because he\u2019ll need it. This is the right course of action, even if that\u2019s a gut-punch for a franchise drunk on success and spoiled by five straight Finals trips . Yes, it\u2019s Nov. 1 and it\u2019s already time to think about next November for the team that won three of the last five NBA titles. Time to envision a retooled Warriors\u2019 team with a healthy Curry, a healed and restless Thompson, a smoldering Draymond, a possible NBA-ready teenager fresh from the Draft lottery and whomever D\u2019Angelo Russell fetches in a trade. It might be enough to make the two Los Angeles teams pause from their death match and take notice. This of course means the Warriors are running the risk of uttering the four-letter T-word that the basketball purists abhor. Well, if you stank, you must tank, and the Warriors without the Splash Brothers are all but guaranteed to reek, even in their new home that still has that new-home aroma. Even with Curry and an abbreviated season from Thompson, the Warriors would\u2019ve scuffled to make the 2020 playoffs in their first season after Kevin Durant. Yes, they\u2019re proud and all that, and you can never underestimate the heart of a champion. Yet this season in the West could belong to LeBron James or Kawhi Leonard \u2014 whomever survives that turf battle. Even in a best-case scenario, the Warriors were a one-(round) and-done in the playoffs. Their first-round pick in 2020 belongs to the Nets if it falls outside the top 20. By understanding if not embracing the reality of the moment , the Warriors can keep their future Hall of Fame backcourt healthy and also maintain their pick (which is likely to fall in the lottery). This team has a history of making wise Draft decisions. This presents a delicious twist: Do you know how hard it is for a team with great players to add a lottery pick? It rarely happens. This is somewhat similar to, though not exactly like, the 1996-97 San Antonio Spurs. They were fresh off 59- and 62-win seasons, but back and foot injuries limited former MVP winner David Robinson to six games that season . When the Spurs started 3-15, then-general manager Gregg Popovich fired and took over for coach Bob Hill. With Robinson put on ice by Christmas , the Spurs went 20-62. They stunned the NBA world in winning the Draft lottery, snagging Tim Duncan and haven\u2019t had a losing season or missed the playoffs since. Coincidentally, the Warriors\u2019 first game without Curry will be Friday against the Spurs ( 10:30 ET, League Pass ), who are now stretching their legacy into a third decade. But that \u201996-97 season hasn\u2019t been forgotten by those still attached to the organization, such as former Spurs legend and current TV analyst Sean Elliott . That season, he was limited to 39 games because of injury. \u201cDavid was such a focal part of the club, that everything we did was predicated on him,\u201d Elliott said. \u201cWhen you lose him, you just can\u2019t plug in another David. It\u2019s partly going to be a little of that without Steph Curry. He\u2019s so much a part of their offense that you can\u2019t replicate that.\u201d With Duncan looming as the game-changing No. 1 pick, the tanking accusations were flying \u2014 and not just in the direction of the Spurs, but others as well. The Boston Celtics held better odds of winning the lottery yet whiffed. Had they won, Rick Pitino might still be coaching in Boston, as Popovich is in San Antonio. Elliott said the T-word was never spoken of in the locker room. \u201cGuys were playing hard,\u201d he said. \u201cIt wasn\u2019t that we were tanking games. It\u2019s just that everybody had more than what we had.\u201d Popovich has advice for Steve Kerr, his friend and former protege, as the Warriors coach braces for the inevitable. \u201cYou don\u2019t have time to react to losing players,\u201d said Popovich. \u201cYou continue to develop the young kids, play the way you need to play to win games but also to teach because they\u2019re going to be there next year, for the most part. And the players who were hurt are going to come back. You can\u2019t just stagnate. You don\u2019t miss a beat. You just keep going.\u201d Kerr has nine new players, most of whom are a work in progress and none bring the championship chops necessary to extend a dynasty. The Warriors\u2019 dynasty likely died when Durant bailed to Brooklyn last summer. Before Curry\u2019s injury, Golden State was trying to merely stay in the playoff conversation this season (and maybe pull a surprise if Thompson returned in early spring). With Curry and Thompson both out for an extended period, the Warriors will likely be buried by then. The blueprint has been hastily rewritten with Jordan Poole and Willie Cauley-Stein and Glenn Robinson III doing heavy lifting. That\u2019s the core right now. And so, why bother playing for today when tomorrow means so much more?  They\u2019ll need to make a decision at some point on Russell, who\u2019s off to a shaky start and won\u2019t have the security blanket of Curry for a chunk of the season at the very least. Do they shop him at the trade deadline? Is he worth more to them in another uniform? It\u2019s always a hard swallow for teams when forced to make a sudden shift in philosophy and not for the better. It\u2019s about lowering expectations (that weren\u2019t steep to begin with) while watching those championship trophies start to gather dust and wondering what the pavement feels like before the fall. The tickets at Chase Center have already been sold and those fans aren\u2019t unrealistic. There\u2019s no need for the Warriors to apologize for the long nights coming their way. They can blame circumstances beyond their control. In certain, dire situations, even teams that don\u2019t try to lose end up losing anyway. This league is about talent. And the once-loaded Warriors, shockingly and suddenly, after five fruitful seasons of living in a make-believe bubble loaded with champagne and championships, are about to learn how the other half lives. * * * More on NBA.com \u2013 Curry out at least 3 months \u2013 LeBron, NBA react to Curry\u2019s injury \u2013 13 takeaways from NBA Roster Survey \u2013 6 early candidates for Kia Sixth Man * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. "},{"id":31018,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/derrick-rose-load-management-era-feature","date":"2019-11-01","title":"If only Derrick Rose had load management","content":" CHICAGO \u2014  Imagine Sandy Koufax with access to Tommy John surgery. Think how much modern orthopedic and training techniques might have helped Bobby Orr, Joe Namath or Gale Sayers. Now picture Derrick Rose in the era of load management. The term that\u2019s all the rage in the NBA these days \u2014 and the source of some controversy, for sitting out healthy players as a means of injury prevention \u2014 didn\u2019t require medical breakthroughs achieved over decades. Load management is simply an approach, a self-discipline by teams in rationing out a player\u2019s usage to maximize his availability by, er, limiting his availability. Rose, alas, arrived six or seven years too soon to benefit from it. Load management didn\u2019t exist as a league-wide trend when he suffered in April 2012 the ACL blowout to his left knee that forever altered his NBA trajectory. \u201cAll the time in Chicago when I was coming back, load management wasn\u2019t a term then,\u201d Rose told NBA.com this week. \u201cBack then, it was, \u2018He\u2019s [expletive] being lazy.\u2019\u201d There were no healthy DNPs back then. Very few at all until San Antonio coach Gregg Popovich began to force the issue with veteran stars Tim Duncan, Manu Ginobili and Tony Parker. The idea spread to those overseeing others such as LeBron James, Joel Embiid and Anthony Davis. Over time, getting random games off became almost a status symbol, signifying membership among the NBA\u2019s elite. Kawhi Leonard\u2019s trade to Toronto heightened the tactic\u2019s profile as the Raptors chased and won the 2019 NBA Finals . Though Leonard sat out 22 games last season, he still was named to the All-NBA second team and finished ninth in MVP balloting. By contrast, when Rose missed 16 games in 2015-16, his final season with the Bulls, the onus still was on him: damaged goods. For the fourth year in a row. \u201cThey expect [you to miss games] now,\u201d Rose said. \u201cThey know, \u2018OK, he\u2019s not going to get through the year [playing 82]. But as long as we get to the playoffs, that\u2019s when we need him.\u2019 It\u2019s funny how things change.\u201d Rose at 22 had become the NBA\u2019s youngest MVP in 2010-11. The next season, in the hurried-up, lockout-shortened schedule, he missed 27 of 66 games, coping with five separate injuries. Then late in Game 1 of the playoffs, he blew out his knee in the first round against Philadelphia. Even the NBA\u2019s view of ACL reconstruction and recovery has changed since then. Players like Golden State\u2019s Klay Thompson essentially are told \u201cSee you in a year,\u201d with anything quicker than that viewed as a bonus. Rose\u2019s timeline was pegged initially at 8-to-10 months, which translated into pressure on him to return in 2012-13. When that didn\u2019t happen, some fans, media folks and even friends inside the Bulls organization began to question his toughness and drive. Interestingly, Rose this week mentioned NFL running back Adrian Peterson as another factor influencing the perception of his rehab. Peterson tore the ACL and MCL in his left knee in December 2011. But he was back in the Minnesota Vikings\u2019 lineup in Week 1 of 2012. He played in all 16 games, rushed for a league-best 2,097 yards and was chosen the NFL\u2019s Most Valuable Player. And here was Rose, taking 17 months between appearances for the Bulls. So what if it was an apples vs. oranges comparison. \u201cEverybody was taking football and kind of translating that over to what was going on with me,\u201d Rose said. \u201cDon\u2019t get me wrong, that\u2019s a helluva accomplishment. But it\u2019s crazy that people tried to compare us.\u201d Fortunately, Rose can look back on his career-altering injury \u2014 and a series of meniscus tears and other ailments in its wake \u2014 from a happier vantage point than, say, Brandon Roy, Jay Williams, Penny Hardaway or Yao Ming. He\u2019s been active, happy, healthy and productive for the Detroit Pistons through their first five games, showing flashes of \u2014 if not his best self \u2014 his steadier, more reliable style arrived at in recent years. Heading into an always anticipated return to Chicago\u2019s United Center Friday, Rose has averaged 20.4 points and 6.2 assists while shooting 55.3 percent off the Pistons\u2019 bench. He had 16 points and 10 assists at Toronto Wednesday, playing less than 21 minutes. And that\u2019s been the key. Whether getting 18 and 10 in the opener, scoring 27 and 31 in Detroit\u2019s next two games or attacking for the winning layup against Indiana Monday, Rose has yet to play as much as 27 minutes. This is load management as minutes restriction, managed nightly. Rose is playing less but more often. \u201cI got to watch his minutes,\u201d Casey told Detroit reporters. \u201cI try to keep his minutes around 27, 28. That limits us to what we can do with him. \u2026 If it\u2019s tight or close, we may fudge the numbers a little bit, but for the most part, we\u2019re going to keep it around that number each and every night.\u201d Casey also said: \u201cI\u2019m not going to sit here and ramp up and ruin a guy\u2019s comeback career by getting excited and playing him 30 minutes and losing him for two or three games.\u201d It\u2019s worth noting, for perspective, how Rose has done \u2014 really \u2014 since his notorious injury. Coming into 2019-20, over 267 games in six seasons split between the Bulls, Knicks, Cavaliers and Timberwolves, Rose had averaged 16.6 points, 3.1 rebounds and 4.3 assists. Admittedly, that\u2019s not up to his All-Star, MVP form of his first four seasons (21.0, 3.8, 6.8). But only 15 guards in the NBA matched or bettered Rose\u2019s averages \u2014 16.6, 3.1, 4.3 \u2014 over the same period. In each of those seasons, those stats were reached or topped by anywhere from 12 to 17 guards. \u201cThat\u2019s my ammunition,\u201d Rose said. \u201cI know I\u2019ve been hooping, but everybody wants to go right to my MVP year.\u201d Rose has been a solid, occasionally electric contributor since then, most recently with the Timberwolves. His 50-point throwback performance on Halloween 2018 was one of the season\u2019s feel-good moments. Rose had three more games for Minnesota scoring at least 30 points, with another 20 scoring 20-29. After doing that on a veteran\u2019s minimum contract, Rose earned a two-year, $15 million payday from Detroit. Rose said he understood why his drop from great to good might not have played so well had he stayed with the Bulls. \u201cI didn\u2019t fault anybody for that,\u201d he said. \u201cI would want my favorite player, too, to come back and have a crazy year.\u201d The Pistons don\u2019t need that. Casey is glad to have an offensive option to what became overreliance last spring on forward Blake Griffin. The team especially has welcomed that with Griffin out so far with a sore hamstring. In a recent interview on SiriusXM\u2019s NBA Radio, former Bulls and Wolves coach Tom Thibodeau spoke excitedly about Rose. \u201cI think he\u2019ll be phenomenal. To persevere through that, when you\u2019ve had to sit out a year with an injury, that\u2019s a tough deal in itself. But to deal with it three consecutive years, I don\u2019t know, I\u2019m just really proud of him.\u201d Asked what he plays for now, compared to a decade ago, Rose mentioned winning and his three children, in leaving a legacy of not quitting. Money isn\u2019t on the list, he said, after more than $120 million in NBA earnings and massive endorsement deals. \u201cAnd I still want to be great,\u201d he added. \u201cThat\u2019s what a lot of people overlook. But that feeling doesn\u2019t go anywhere. I still want to go out there and prove to people I can hoop. I know I\u2019ve been through a lot, but again, me going out and setting an example, I think it helps a lot of people.\u201d Playing Rose off the bench behind Reggie Jackson and even fill-in starter Tim Frazier, Detroit wants to keep the 31-year-old guard healthy and locked into his role. If it holds all season, Rose would have a chance to match what only one other NBA MVP ever has done: Reinventing himself from the league\u2019s best player to its top reserve. \u201cI know who it is \u2014 Bill Walton,\u201d Rose said. The legendary UCLA center and Portland Trail Blazers star won his MVP award in 1978. After being waylaid by chronic foot issues in subsequent seasons, Walton helped Boston off the bench to the 1986 NBA title and was named Sixth Man of the Year. If Lou Williams for whatever reason loosens his grip on the SMOY award, Rose could snag it \u2014 if he\u2019s fulfilled by coming off the bench all season. \u201cYeah, yeah, it\u2019s whatever the team wants,\u201d he said. \u201cWinning takes care of every area. If we win, I could be the second. \u201cMy biggest thing is just trying to push these guys with a certain amount of energy and effort every game. And to teach the young guys, taking on the challenge of being vocal, which will help me. Trying to learn in every area that I can.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. The views on this page do not necessarily reflect the views of the NBA, its clubs or Turner Broadcasting."},{"id":31020,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-things-have-been-ghosted","date":"2019-10-31","title":"17 NBA things that have been ghosted from memory","content":" On a night traditionally known more for tricks and treats than picks and rolls, it seems appropriate to do a little ghost hunting, NBA-style. We\u2019re not talking the Ghost Ballers of BIG3 fame or even the Skirvin Hilton Hotel in Oklahoma City, a stop on the circuit that some teams claim is actually haunted . We\u2019re thinking of things that used to be, gone-but-not-forgotten aspects of the league that lurk in the memory, even if they\u2019re never coming back. Here in no particular order are some Halloween hoops hobgoblins that fall somewhere on the scary scale between the chain-rattling Jacob Marley and Casper: 1. Long-gone arenas . Oracle Arena, so recently vacated by the Golden State Warriors, is the latest addition to the NBA\u2019s long list of abandoned homes. Many are gone themselves, though you still can catch a glimpse now and then on Hardwood Classics. There are too many to list, due to NBA teams moving on up to bigger, better digs over time. But a sampling would include the Cow Palace, Cobo Arena, Chicago Stadium, Boston Garden, The Forum, L.A. Sports Arena, Milwaukee\u2019s MECCA, the Salt Palace, McNichols Arena, HemisFair Arena, Market Square, the Summit, the Spectrum, the Omni, the Pyramid, ARCO Arena\/Sleep Train Arena and on and on. 2. Belted shorts . Relegated to the throwback bin, along with the more recent sleeved jerseys. 3. The six-foot lane . Heck, the 12-foot lane. The former was widened in 1951 in response to Minneapolis big man George Mikan\u2019s dominance. Then it was widened again in 1964 to its current 16 feet in hopes of tamping down Wilt Chamberlain\u2019s impact. 4. Commercial air travel . Some things on a used-to-be list inspire nostalgia in those who experienced them and curiosity in those who didn\u2019t. But it\u2019s highly unlikely any former or current players and coaches would swap today\u2019s luxury charter flights for the way the NBA used to travel. Wake-up calls at 5 a.m. for the first flight out. Waiting out delays at the gate with the beat writers and civilians. Seven-footers folding themselves into economy class seating. 5. Obstacle-course schedules . The NBA in recent years has tried to be responsive to players\u2019 performance needs and physical limitations, working to minimize the number of back-to-back games and four-in-five-night stretches. Didn\u2019t used to be that way. Consider the Baltimore Bullets, who in January 1966 were put through these paces: Games in St. Louis, Detroit, back to St. Louis, day off, to Philadelphia, to Boston, home vs. Lakers. A week later, they bounced back and forth between L.A. (Lakers) and San Francisco for four games in four nights, then traveled to New York to face the Knicks for their fifth game in five nights. Baltimore\u2019s record in those 11 games: 2-9. 6. Doubleheaders . Some teams in the NBA\u2019s first few decades would book a Harlem Globetrotters exhibition as the night\u2019s opening attraction. But the biggies were when the Knicks would host at Madison Square Garden a neutral-site game for two other NBA clubs. A lingering memory for some who attended: The thick haze that hung over the arena\u2019s upper reaches, courtesy of the smokers puffing away all evening. 7. Tape-delay. It seems inconceivable in 2019 that an NBA playoff game, never mind a Finals contest, might be shown on anything but live TV. Nope. The league didn\u2019t have much leverage in the late 1970s, before Magic Johnson and Larry Bird arrived to help goose interest and ratings. Networks forced fans to stay up late to watch games that were off before the telecasts tipped off. The practice continued into the \u201880s, with four of six Finals games in 1981 held till 11:30 p.m. ET. Michael Jordan was already creating new fans when the last tape-delayed game, Game 3 of the West finals between the Lakers and Rockets , aired on Friday, May 16, 1986. 8. \u201cIllegal!\u201d That used to be a frequent bellow from the league\u2019s benches, with coaches trying to alert the refs when opposing defenses breached (or didn\u2019t) the complicated illegal defense rules. The NBA purged most of that around the turn of the century by legislating in zone play . 9. Shattered backboards . For a while, it seemed as if backboards were exploding every few weeks in the Association. Darryl (\u201cChocolate Thunder\u201d) Dawkins was the most avid crack-titioner, getting two in 1979. The earliest recorded instance came in 1946, when a Celtics forward named Chuck Connors (later more famous as TV\u2019s \u201cRifleman\u201d) shattered one during warmups . Baltimore\u2019s Gus Johnson is said to have shattered three . Shaquille O\u2019Neal didn\u2019t get the glass but twice got entire support structures, pulling the backboards down to the court in his rookie season. In March 1993 , against Chicago, New Jersey\u2019s Chris Morris dunked and shattered a board without glass falling to the floor . 10. Three to make two . That old free-throw bonus was abolished by 1981-82. It made the game drag, and Jerry Colangelo, then GM of the Suns and the chairman of the NBA\u2019s competition committee, rightly said: \u201cPro players shouldn\u2019t need that extra foul shot.\u201d 11. Phantom franchises . Oooh, pretty scary, kids, when you think of all the teams that are no more. They are rattling around in the mind long after they were supposedly dead and buried. We\u2019re not talking just about the antiquities such as the Indianapolis Olympians, the Washington Capitols or the Toronto Huskies. The spirits of the Seattle SuperSonics, Buffalo Braves, San Diego Clippers and Vancouver Grizzlies still walk the NBA earth. Then there are most of the ABA franchises \u2014 Virginia Squires, Utah Stars, Kentucky Colonels, Spirits of St. Louis \u2014 that died more than 40 years ago before or in the merger .  12. Hand checking . A lot of capable defenders had their effectiveness vaporized overnight when the laying on of hands vs. a ball handler was outlawed in 2004 . The NBA, in case you hadn\u2019t noticed, likes scoring. 13. Injury shenanigans . As silly or frustrating as labels like \u201cDNP-Old\u201d or \u201cload management\u201d seem today, the reporting of injuries real or feigned used to be much less authentic. Before the inactive list, there was \u201cinjured reserve,\u201d to which NBA teams would designate up to two players. Anyone put on that list was sidelined for a minimum of five games, and with smaller roster sizes in effect, it was a handy place to stash guys. So there was a whole lot of tendinitis and plantar fasciitis going on. This practice was snuffed in 2005-06. 14. \u201cPlay on!\u201d Like the force-out ruling, this is a remnant of the days when the referees had and used more discretion in working their games. If a player lost the ball out of bounds but his elbow was knocked by a foe, the force-out meant the ball handler\u2019s team retained possession. \u201cPlay on!\u201d was a frequent order barked by refs when certain contact or violations were deemed minimally intrusive. Heavier scrutiny of the game officials\u2019 performance and, later, video reviews now try to adjudicate everything down to the tip of a fingernail. 15. The 2-3-2 Finals format . This was adopted in 1985 as a reaction to those Lakers-Celtics or Lakers-Sixers championship series, which had the NBA universe crossing the country four or five times in a span of two weeks. Suggestions that the league was being energy-conscious, in terms of jet fuel, were part of it, too. The practice fiddled some with the notion of home-court advantage, although MLB continues to use it for its World Series. With charter flights deployed by all teams, league execs and even some of the media, the NBA changed back to the 2-2-1-1-1 format in 2014 to align with its postseasons\u2019 earlier rounds. 16. Player-coaches . Forty men in NBA history have done it. The first was Ed Sadowski of the Toronto Huskies in the Basketball Association of America precursor to the NBA. Only two men won championships as player-coaches: Baltimore\u2019s Buddy Jeannette in 1948 and Boston\u2019s Bill Russell in 1968 and 1969. The youngest player coach ever was Dave DeBusschere , who took over the Pistons in 1964 at age 24 (not long after ending his second career as an MLB pitcher). The Hawks\u2019 Richie Guerin logged the most games (372) in the role, yet was named Coach of the Year in the one season in the middle when he stopped playing. Legend Lenny Wilkens was a player-coach for two teams, spending three seasons at it in Seattle and one in Portland. And the last player-coach in NBA history was Dave Cowens, who accepted the gig after coach Satch Sanders got fired in 1978-79. None of the players wanted to learn a new system, Cowens said, so \u201cI kind of took one for the team.\u201d The practice died with the arrival of the salary cap in 1984, with NBA brass wary that paying a coaching bonus might enable a team to circumvent the cap. 17. Victory cigars . For obvious reasons. Probably victory vaping, too. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . Davis had 40 points and 20 rebounds in just 30 minutes on Tuesday night in the Lakers\u2019 120-91 blowout win against the Memphis Grizzlies. In logging that performance, he became the sixth Lakers player to notch a 40-20 game. Elgin Baylor, Wilt Chamberlain, Kareem Abdul-Jabbar, George Mikan and Shaquille O\u2019Neal \u2014 each of them Hall of Famers \u2014 all accomplished the feat with the Lakers. O\u2019Neal was the last to do so when he put up 48 points and 20 rebounds in 39 minutes against the Boston Celtics on March 21, 2003 . \u201cIt\u2019s an honor to be on that list with those legends but more important is we got the win,\u201d Davis said. \u201cIt was a grind in the first half and my teammates trusted me. I just tried to be a monster on the glass.\u201d A big part of Davis getting to that stat line came via free throws, where he shot 26-for-27. For perspective, the Grizzlies attempted 23 free throws as a team in last night\u2019s game. Per Elias Sports Bureau, Davis became the first player in NBA history to record at least 40 points and 20 rebounds in 32 minutes or less. The previous low was held by Baylor, who had 46 points and 22 rebounds in 33 minutes against the Detroit Pistons in 1961 . Davis is also the fourth player in league history and first since Michael Jordan in 1987 to make 26 or more free throws. The all-time record for free throws made in a game is held by Chamberlain. He sank 28 of them en route to his famous 100-point game against the New York Knicks played in Hershey, Pa in 1962. Davis also set an NBA record for most free throws made in a quarter when he sank 18 (out of 18 attempts) in the third quarter . ( Lakers.com\u2019s Rodrigo Azurmendi also points out that Davis was even fouled by players from five different countries \u2014 the United States, Serbia, Brazil, Canada and Lithuania.) Aside from those feats at the free-throw line, Davis also joined O\u2019Neal and Abdul-Jabbar as the third Lakers player with 100 points, 10 blocks and 10 assists through his first four games ( per ESPN ). Davis was questionable two hours before the game due to a right shoulder injury suffered in Sunday\u2019s win over Charlotte. He did some dribbling and shooting on the court before being cleared. He had 16 points and nine rebounds in the first quarter but went back to the locker room at the start of the second to get the shoulder checked and re-taped. Coach Frank Vogel thought he might have to go the rest of the game without Davis until he saw him come back to the bench. After the game, Davis said his shoulder was still, but he thinks it will improve since the Lakers have a couple days off. At 3-1, the Lakers are off to their best start since the 2010-11 season and will play again Friday when they visit the Dallas Mavericks ( 9:30 ET, ESPN ). (Editor\u2019s Note: The following 1-on-1 conversation has been condensed and edited). * * * NBA.com : Have Dwyane Wade, Dirk Nowitzki or Kobe Bryant given you any advice for this farewell tour? Vince Carter:  Nah, not yet. I plan on talking to some of my guys when I see them. But honestly, I\u2019m just approaching it as another year. It\u2019s still my job. I can probably honestly say whenever it\u2019s over I\u2019ll be like, \u201cDang, I wish I valued or cherished it more,\u201d but at the same time I am valuing it and cherishing it because I\u2019m doing what I love in the moment. That\u2019s what I love doing. It\u2019s kind of easy to approach it that way just because that\u2019s what I enjoy. Which games are you most looking forward to during this final season? All of my former stops. [Playing] my former teams is going to be fun and exciting. It\u2019ll be more emotions than nerves. I had great memories in every stop that I\u2019ve played at so I think I\u2019ll have appreciation. With all your 1998 draft classmates retired, who are some current players that you have a close relationship with? Kyle Lowry is one of them. Kent Bazemore. Jae Crowder. I know I\u2019m going to forget some people, but those are some of the guys that I talk to the most that are current players. And there\u2019s probably more, I\u2019m gonna hate myself later on. But those are the ones I talk to the most right now where I can think of in the last two, three weeks I\u2019ve spoken to those guys. Speaking of that Draft, take me through that night when you found out you were being traded for your college teammate Antawn Jamison. Literally, [former NBA commissioner David Stern] shook my hand. We took the picture. And he said, \u201cJust stay right here, there\u2019s about to be a trade.\u201d So I\u2019m back there like, damn somebody\u2019s about to get traded . Antawn was sitting at the bottom of the steps. He was trying to tell me that we\u2019re about to get traded, but I was like, \u201cWhat, what, what?\u201d It was so much going on because I was on stage. So when [Stern] said, \u201cThe Toronto Raptors have traded the rights \u2026\u201d I was like, damn that\u2019s what he was saying . In just one word, how would you describe your legendary dunk in the 2000 Olympics over Frederic Weis? Clueless. I didn\u2019t know I had dunked over him the entire game so I was clueless. What was it like going head-to-head against Allen Iverson in that legendary 2001 playoff series? Going against him brought the best out of me. As far as that playoff series, it was probably one of the best in my career. I remember Game 1 just having to be sharp. I knew I had to bring it after obviously playing him in the season. I think he lit us up for 50 a couple times. So I knew what to expect. I didn\u2019t have to be out of character, but I had to play well. I was the center of attention for [the Raptors] as he was for the Sixers. I knew I had to score, and that didn\u2019t mean going shot for shot, point for point. Couldn\u2019t do that. Allen Iverson is Allen Iverson. So if he scored 55, 56, I just needed to be solid to where we could win. I think I had 42 the first game, a good night. When he scored 54 going into Game 2, my response was that we couldn\u2019t get too far behind on this team. [Both teams] felt like the winner of that series could go to The Finals. No disrespect to Milwaukee. (Editor\u2019s note: Carter scored 35 in Game 1, but responded to Iverson\u2019s 54 points in Game 2 with a 50-point game in Game 3.) Take me through your emotions the day of Game 7. I\u2019d say it was bittersweet, but it seemed more like sweetbitter. You go to your college graduation that morning and happily earn your degree, but ended it with missing the game-winner and losing the series. It was a great day. It was a lot going on. I wouldn\u2019t change it. I would do it the same way again. It was one of those days where I was able to accomplish a goal \u2014 a life-long goal, a family goal, a goal that any college student and educator would look forward to. And I wanted to cap it off by having the ultimate day. Not many people can say they hit a game-winning shot in Game 7 against the 76ers on the biggest stage. Yeah, it\u2019s crazy how one shot can completely change a narrative. Yeah, and it was sad and a shame to hear and read some people say \u201cit\u2019s just a degree\u201d or \u201cyou could buy that degree\u201d or \u201cwhat\u2019s the big deal in walking [across the stage]?\u201d That just doesn\u2019t make sense. I walk through my front door and see my diploma every day, and that\u2019s something that I\u2019m proud of. Because when [basketball] is over, I still got this. I come from a family of educators. All of my family [members] are teachers of some sort in the education system. Who was your favorite athlete to battle over your career? T-Mac. Kobe. I played together with these guys. Kobe and I played AAU ball. T-Mac and I were obviously family, so it\u2019s nothing like going against your superstar cousin. You can\u2019t beat that. Take me through your decision to give up your starting spot to Michael Jordan in the 2003 All-Star Game in his last season. We got to All-Star weekend and I had a brief conversation with David Stern and we kind of talked about it, but I felt there was nothing to talk about. That\u2019s just a no-brainer for me to let MJ [start]. I said the problem is going to be you guys convincing him. I just had a feeling he wouldn\u2019t go for it. I kind of briefly mentioned it to him and said, \u201cHey man, you\u2019re starting.\u201d He said, \u201cNo, you earned that.\u201d So right before the lineups I said, \u201cMJ, you are starting. Point blank period. You\u2019re starting.\u201d And I told him I was going to walk to the back so he couldn\u2019t make me start because I wasn\u2019t going to be there. We went back and forth. He goes out there. I felt like once they called his name he had to go. Are you hoping to be an honorary All-Star this season? No, no. If I earn it, give it to me. But that\u2019s just me. Don\u2019t take this the wrong way when I say it like that. That\u2019s just who I am. I\u2019m very appreciative of earning my All-Star spots, being a leading vote-getter, so I don\u2019t know. I just have a hard time with it. We\u2019ll see if later down the line my view changes. You ranked your dunk over Alonzo Mourning as your favorite dunk of all-time. Take me through that moment. I remember just going up. I felt since he was under the rim if I could get up in the air before him, I had a chance because even if he knocked me back my momentum could still take me towards the rim. But when he hit me, he hit me upward, which put me up higher by the rim. So I\u2019m just looking at the rim in a different view, thinking I can\u2019t miss. You see I tried to play it cool, but inside I was like a 7-year-old. I was just thinking how that\u2019s Alonzo Mourning, one of the best shot blockers in the history of the game. What are the biggest \u201cwhat if\u201d moments you have when you think about your career? What if I did make that shot [against the Sixers]? What if I did? What happens next? I don\u2019t know. What if T-Mac and I had a chance to play together longer? I got another one. What if we don\u2019t lose to Boston in six back when I was in Orlando? Cause we had a chance. They ended up going to The Finals. That was my other opportunity so I wonder what if. I always wondered that. Yeah, what were your thoughts when you found out you were leaving New Jersey to go back home and play in your hometown of Orlando? I don\u2019t think people know this story but the day I got traded to the Orlando Magic was the same day Michael Jackson died. June 25th, 2009. So, I was doing my basketball camp and my brother called me. He told me [about the trade] and we were excited. Then, me and a couple of my boys were at dinner and they\u2019re saying, \u201cOh man, that\u2019s crazy you\u2019re coming back home.\u201d So we\u2019re excited and the lady at the restaurant was like, \u201cHow can you be excited?\u201d Social media wasn\u2019t around like that. We didn\u2019t know. We\u2019re just hype about the trade. So my boy\u2019s like, \u201cYou heard the news too?\u201d She goes, \u201cHow can you be excited about that? The world is grieving at this point.\u201d He says, \u201cWhat are you talking about? My man just got traded to the Magic.\u201d That\u2019s when she says, \u201cMichael Jackson died.\u201d And we were like, \u201cWhat?!\u201d How do you connect with the younger generation these days? I read where NFL star Larry Fitzgerald said it\u2019s a lot different than it was 10 years ago. You have to listen and learn first and foremost. And we talk basketball so that\u2019s how it organically branches out to things like styles of music. As an older guy, you kind of just adapt to new styles more so than [the younger players] adapting to me. We have to adapt. Larry and I, Tom Brady, we have to adapt to what\u2019s around us. How many young players have called you Mr. Carter? A few. I\u2019m like just call me Vince (laughs). It\u2019s crazy. What advice would you give to someone like Zion Williamson, who came into the league being labeled a dunker by some? Be yourself. He\u2019s two years removed from high school. Players get to the NBA and we expect them to be somebody that they need to develop themselves to be. I came in labeled as a dunker, and then some people would say, \u201cYeah I knew you could shoot a little bit, but I want to see you dunk.\u201d Just like right now, when you see Zion, you don\u2019t want to see him shoot a jump shot. You want to see him dunk unless he\u2019s playing against your favorite team. And then you say what? \u201cMake him shoot a jump shot.\u201d But if you\u2019re just a fan of his, what are you gonna say? \u201cI want to see him dunk. I want to see him dunk on somebody.\u201d That\u2019s the natural reality of it. So just be yourself, play your game. [People] don\u2019t even know that he\u2019s got a decent handle. Not a bad passer. Shot-blocker. Yeah he\u2019s got all that. When we played [the Pelicans], I told him to be yourself and let all that other stuff take care of itself when it happens. Don\u2019t try to come out and be someone you\u2019re not. Then what happens? They\u2019re gonna consider him a bust. I would just be me. Everything else is gonna take care of itself. I knew that people were going to see that I could shoot, score and pass the ball. I just had to be patient, but it\u2019s not for everybody. Some people feel like they have to prove because of what\u2019s being said on social media. I ain\u2019t have that. You\u2019ve been fortunate to still get calls from teams at this point in your career. Why do you think Carmelo Anthony hasn\u2019t gotten the same chance? Situations are different. I think it\u2019s just timing at this point. I definitely think he deserves to be in the NBA. He\u2019s one of the most prolific scorers this league has seen at many levels. Pure scorer. I think in time a team will grab him, a playoff team who needs a scorer with his ability. If he\u2019s willing to come off the bench, I think he\u2019ll help a team with his starters mentality. What kept you from ring chasing towards the end of your career like some guys do? I can\u2019t. I just can\u2019t. I didn\u2019t come into my career like that. Guys who see things now see things different. They\u2019re exposed to things a little different. The way the game is played, showed and understood 20 years ago isn\u2019t like now. So I just naturally adapt to that. So when Trae [Young] is in his 15th, 20th year, what\u2019s he gonna know? He\u2019s not gonna know what I knew and how it was. He and young guys coming in now are going to know this era. That\u2019s just the way it is. What does Vince Carter want to be remembered by? I love to play. I love to play. People ask, \u201cWhy are you doing this, why are you doing that?\u201d Because I love playing. If I didn\u2019t love this anymore \u2014 stuff like drills and all that \u2014 then I wouldn\u2019t do it. I just love to play. Obviously, you saw the smiles and me having fun as a young guy when I came into the league. At 42, nothing\u2019s changed. Still love to play. Still love to be here. I\u2019m playing with a young team that\u2019s probably not going to win a championship this year, but I still love to play and compete. I enjoy it. * * *"},{"id":31040,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/things-know-nba-oct-29","date":"2019-10-29","title":"4 NBA things to know for Oct. 29","content":" Get up to speed on the latest NBA news, plus a quick look at stories we\u2019ll be following closely today: 1. The Luka & Kristaps show in Denver: Dallas has lived up to its hype thus far as a must-watch NBA League Pass squad and slowing down Luka Doncic and Kristaps Porzingis has not been easy. The Mavs visit the undefeated Nuggets tonight ( 9 ET, League Pass ), who will likely have to use a variety of bodies \u2014 both big and small \u2014 to contain the Mavs\u2019 star duo. 2. Welcome aboard, Jimmy: The Miami Heat have held down the fort while their big offseason addition, Jimmy Butler, delayed his debut because of the birth of his child . He will be suiting up tonight as the Heat host the Hawks ( 7:30 ET, NBA TV ) in what might end up being a key early-season showdown in the Southeast Division. 3. Late-night excitement in L.A.:  This three-game Tuesday ends with a dandy as the young, exciting Grizzlies visit the title-minded Lakers ( 10:30 ET, NBA TV ). Grizzlies guard Ja Morant showed out in Sunday\u2019s victory (and toe-to-toe battle with Kyrie Irving) at home. How will he fare tonight in his first matchup with LeBron James, Anthony Davis and Co.? 4. Remember when \u2026: To somewhat quote the immortal Ferris Bueller, life moves pretty fast \u2014 both overall and in the NBA. That\u2019s how we\u2019re left feeling this morning in knowing today is the 16th anniversary of Chris Bosh, LeBron James and Carmelo Anthony making their debut in the league."},{"id":31068,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/mark-leonard-kawhi-leonard-feature","date":"2019-10-29","title":"Looking for closure","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014 Sundown in Compton, on a busy boulevard, where the beat is thumping from cars passing by, windows open. It\u2019s typical for these streets, basically, especially after 6 p.m. Working class folks are unwinding and headed home, except for those at M&M Star Car Wash and Detailing, where a dozen weary employees have just enough energy left to shoot a collective eye-roll in the direction of their otherwise beloved boss. They just overheard his brief phone conversation with someone running late: \u201cMan, we\u2019re \u2018bout to close, but bring it real quick,\u201d a common response from a businessman who kept the cash register and the customer happy. Whenever the workers are ready to punch the clock there\u2019s always someone driving in trying to beat it, and that\u2019s when Mark Leonard \u2014 they called him by his nickname, \u201cMick\u201d \u2014 tells his staff: \u201cWe\u2019ll do one more.\u201d And they answer: \u201c Mick, you always say one more.\u201d As the small and soiled pickup truck arrived and received a scrubbing, Leonard and his wife, Jacquelyne, who worked in the back office handling the books, stood on the lot at 413 North Wilmington, ready to lock up for the night, yet still caught up in the afterglow from the day before. That\u2019s when she told him he was going to be a father again; each had children from previous relationships but this was their first together as a couple after trying for years. He was thrilled. That night, he broke the news to relatives and then fetched her favorite fruits from the grocery. He wanted her to eat healthy the next nine months. \u201cWith the kids, he was a teddy bear,\u201d she said, \u201cand with me, he gave me everything.\u201d   One of Leonard\u2019s other children, a son, would be playing a high school basketball tournament in about an hour and Leonard feared the evening rush on the 405 Freeway. And just then: Someone else appeared on the lot and approached quickly, not by car, but by footstep, and with a strut. \u201cWho in the hell?\u201d Jacquelyne remembers saying. Mark Leonard came from the South Side of Chicago, then was raised and lived most of his entire adult life in and around Compton. People with that geographical bloodline usually carry a gene for detecting danger. His sixth sense did not betray him this day; indeed, the man reached for a handgun under his shirt and aimed. The first shot sent Leonard stumbling and the employees scattering. He told his wife to run and pushed her toward the office. She did not fall; she stayed steady on her feet, actually, and did as she was told. Her husband was right behind her. Until he wasn\u2019t. \u201cI ran into the building and when I realized he wasn\u2019t with me, I ran back and stood at the window and watched, and the guy was standing over him and shooting him,\u201d she says. When the pistol emptied, the gunman turned to her, then turned away and disappeared down the block. At 43, Mark Leonard was a husky man, 6-foot-3 and pushing 300 pounds by his wife\u2019s estimation, a body built from playing football at nearby Banning High School and layered by her tacos. But he couldn\u2019t survive multiple gunshot wounds, not that the punctures discouraged a shaken wife from reacting reflexively after rushing out the building. She collapsed on him, tears mixing with blood, then begged him. \u201cGet up,\u201d she said. \u201cYou got to get up.\u201d And: \u201cWhat about the baby?\u201d * * * There are over 18,000 murder cases cramming the digital library at the Los Angeles County Sheriff\u2019s Department and roughly half are unsolved. When a case stalls, it sits until detectives receive what\u2019s known in investigative parlance as \u201cthe magic phone call,\u201d meaning, a tipster who helps blow the dust off that particular whodunit. But that could be weeks, months, years, even decades \u2014 if ever. In Compton, glorified as the birthplace of gangsta rap, a South-Central township of 100,000 proud residents who grapple with an exhausting history of crime and gang violence, the unsolved rate is among California\u2019s highest. Recent studies show 59% of killers get away with murder. Compton is home to Adams Mortuary , believed to be the country\u2019s only drive-thru funeral home, with a bullet-proof glass partition, which became necessary because a rise in cemetery shootouts made gang members skittish about paying their respects. One particular case is now 11 years old and stayed untouched until this summer. There is renewed interest and buzz in the Mark Leonard case and partly because the son whose high school game the father never made on Jan. 18, 2008 is a two-time NBA Finals MVP and now with the LA Clippers . In a quirky twist, Kawhi Leonard could be a factor in his father\u2019s case all because he became superb at basketball, and as a free agent last summer signed with one of L.A.\u2019s hometown teams, citing a desire to be closer to friends and family as a reason.  \u201cJust to be able to have them drive to the games and watch me play and see them afterward is going to be great,\u201d he said the day he was officially introduced as a Clipper. Kawhi was 16 and a high school junior when Mark Leonard was slain and seemingly not on the path to beating LeBron James and Steph Curry for championships back then; all he had in common with his current self was his now-trademark cornrows. Although Kawhi was a late-rising star among Southern California prep players, the chatter he generated was strictly regional and he eventually signed with San Diego State, not one of the nation\u2019s basketball powerhouse schools. But now, as an NBA superstar, savior of the Clippers and future Hall of Famer? \u201cKawhi\u2019s popularity can help,\u201d says Shaun McCarthy, a detective in the Unsolved Unit. \u201cHe wasn\u2019t famous when his dad died. But even some of the baddest criminals may be sympathetic to Kawhi, who is beginning to do good things in the community. Maybe someone out there says, `I didn\u2019t know that was Kawhi\u2019s dad\u2019 and tells us something. This happens often in high profile cases. Look, it\u2019s all `what-ifs\u2019 and `maybes\u2019. Maybe someone in trouble with the law knows about this murder and may be more willing to provide that now, knowing it will give him consideration in his case. They may benefit by giving up information.\u201d McCarthy said the process of interviewing witnesses and exploring new angles has already begun for other reasons he hesitates to divulge, citing the ongoing nature of the case. \u201cI\u2019ve decided, `Let\u2019s investigate these things,\u2019\u201d he said. \u201cWe can either put it to bed or maybe solve these things. It\u2019s a long shot, but I\u2019m optimistic we can identify some people.\u201d Mark Leonard\u2019s murder was not caused by attempted robbery. When victims are shot multiple times \u2014 10 in this case \u2014 that reflects a revenge hit. Investigators are retracing the curious events in the hours leading up to the shooting. Mark Leonard was paid a visit that morning by someone authorities identified and described as a local gang member with a criminal history for interstate drug transportation, seeking his advice about a recent botched deal with another gang. The two knew each other, although Jacquelyne Leonard said her husband was not in that business. \u201cMark had changed his life totally when I married him because I couldn\u2019t live like that,\u201d she said. \u201cMy mom was a retired judge and my dad was a cop. Mark made an honest living. He built this car wash from the ground up in 2006 and took pride in it. He paved the lot with his bare hands. Put in wide-screen TVs and installed flood lights so we could wash cars at night. Business was booming. We were black-owned. The community came out and supported us. It was a beautiful thing. The customers all knew and liked him because although he was big and intimidating and you couldn\u2019t come to him with no BS, he was a nice guy.\u201d McCarthy said: \u201cMark would\u2019ve never been in this situation if this guy, who was an associate, hadn\u2019t crossed him and used his name.\u201d Hours after that meeting, three other men arrived and spoke to Leonard outside the building. There was a heated discussion that involved shouting, loud enough to bring his wife from the office. \u201cWhen I came out and turned the corner, Mark had pushed this (Latino) guy,\u201d she said. \u201cCome to find out he was in a gang, and you can\u2019t do that. That was a deal breaker from my understanding. Mark went to hit him. I said, \u2018Mark don\u2019t do that.\u2019 He didn\u2019t hit him and they jumped into the car and left.\u201d The L.A. County Sheriff\u2019s Department detective originally assigned to the case was Frank Salerno, now two years retired from the force. Salerno is the son of Frank Sr., a legend in the department for cracking some of L.A.\u2019s most notorious serial killer cases, chief among them the Hillside Strangler , where victims were stashed in the hills surrounding Los Angeles; and the \u201cNight Stalker\u201d Richard Ramirez, who received 13 death sentences for particularly heinous murders. The Leonard case frustrated Frank Jr., who followed his father into the department and worked in homicide and also the gang unit as a lead detective for 34 years. Getting information at the car wash then proved to be futile. \u201cYou kind of get numb to it and used to it after you do it for a while,\u201d he said recently. \u201cThis was a typical case we would handle all the time. And the level of cooperation from witnesses was standard for that area. It\u2019s very rare when we get to a scene where people want to tell us exactly what happened. It\u2019s not like people didn\u2019t talk to us here; we think they didn\u2019t tell us everything they saw because of fear of gang retaliation. Some cases, people won\u2019t even talk, period. You go to a party and everybody was in the bathroom at the time. It\u2019s amazing how many people can fit into a bathroom. The standard answer is, \u2018I was in the bathroom and didn\u2019t see anything.\u2019 \u201d That\u2019s changing. While Leonard ran errands after the argument, Jacquelyne and the employees noticed a car circling the block multiple times. When Leonard returned, it was business as usual right up until the late customer drove on the lot at closing time. Police believe one of the three men who confronted Leonard earlier that day was the shooter and connected to a Latino gang. As detectives began reconnecting the dots, they phoned the widow out of the blue; she has lived without closure for more than a decade. A resolution, however challenging that may be, would give her the answers to the whom and the why. \u201cIt would be great,\u201d she said. \u201cI have prayed 11 years. My life changed drastically in one night.\u201d * * *  The car wash did much labor by hand, and this is where Mark Leonard helped seed Kawhi\u2019s way to NBA stardom, by injecting a work ethic in his son that\u2019s perhaps unsurpassed in the league. Kawhi lived with his mother, Kim Robertson, in Moreno Valley after his parents split when he was five. But he spent some weekends and parts of his summers in Compton with his father on the job, where he washed cars as a teenager \u2014 his hands were unusually large even then \u2014 alongside his two half-brothers, Cameron and Marcus, when he didn\u2019t have a game. \u201cMark told them if they wanted to wear the new tennis shoes, they had to work for them, that he can\u2019t keep buying them stuff,\u201d Jacquelyne Leonard said. \u201cKawhi never complained. He was a prankster at times but a very quiet child and a great kid who listened to his father and respected him.\u201d Kawhi was better at football initially; he played tight end at Canyon Springs High School and was already 6-foot-3, bruising and breaking through tacklers. But his love for basketball grew as he blossomed. His father was heartbroken when the son dropped football after his freshman year. Eventually Mark Leonard made peace and helped train him. By then Kawhi transferred to King High School in Riverside County , and after one practice, the coach at King, Tim Sweeney, called his dad, a legendary prep coach in Riverside, and said: \u201cI\u2019ve got a kid who\u2019s gonna be an NBA All-Star.\u201d Sweeney adds today: \u201cI told other people that same thing, and they all laughed.\u201d Kawhi\u2019s jump shot was flat when he arrived at King; however, the instincts that allow him to roam the floor and make snap decisions on both ends were evident then. His basketball IQ soared. Mostly, the wood-chopping energy was already rooted, a byproduct of the example his father set. \u201cAbsolute crazy\u201d is how Sweeney describes it. \u201cTo be at the level he is now, you have to have the talent but also the work ethic and mindset that\u2019s harder than everybody else\u2019s. I can\u2019t tell you how many times I\u2019d close the doors to our gym so I can go home and see my family, and when I turn the alarm on, the doors are open again. He was always finding a way to get into the gym to play, even at night when he wasn\u2019t supposed to be there.\u201d Sweeney was at dinner when he learned about Kawhi\u2019s father. King had just finished a league game that Mark Leonard never made. At Sweeney\u2019s request, Marvin Lea, a former King star and Kawhi\u2019s AAU coach, opened his home to Kawhi that night and consoled him. \u201cHe really didn\u2019t show no emotions about it,\u201d Lea said, \u201cand if you didn\u2019t know the boy, you wouldn\u2019t know what just happened. If you were around him enough, you know he\u2019s a little different. Kawhi is a private person, then and now. Kawhi handled it through basketball.\u201d The next night, King played the city high school heavyweight, Dominguez, at UCLA\u2019s Pauley Pavilion. Sweeney spoke with Kawhi earlier that day, told him it was his choice to play and would support him if he sat the rest of that season. \u201cLo and behold,\u201d Sweeney said, \u201che shows up with his mom, his uncle Dennis Robertson, all the family is there. I told the people running the event not to have a moment of silence. This kid is holding it together barely, I thought, and to do that, we\u2019re going to lose him. The idiots didn\u2019t listen.\u201d Leonard did remain remarkably composed, scored 17 points in a game King lost, 68-60 , but rushed into his mother\u2019s arms right after the buzzer and sobbed as he squeezed her. Friends had never seen Kawhi shed tears before. \u201cHe was playing for the love of his father and it was the first time he really felt the pain and the loss,\u201d said Sweeney. \u201cHis father was just a very hard-working man who came to as many games as he could; living in Compton, that\u2019s a good hour and a half drive in traffic away from King. He was always very cordial and respectful. He did a good job helping to raise Kawhi.\u201d It was apparent to everyone who knew Kawhi that the court became his sanctuary. In his senior year, he went next-level as a player. With a more polished and airy jump shot, combined with blue-collar energy, he averaged 22.6 points with 13.1 rebounds, 3.9 assists and three blocks and was named Player of the Year in California . Along with Tony Snell, now with the Pistons, Leonard led King to a 30-3 record and the state championship over top-ranked Mater Dei. Thus, the unexpected launch of an NBA superstar began: He played two years at San Diego State, was acquired by the Spurs via a Draft night trade in 2011 . He won an NBA championship and Finals MVP there, then repeated the feat last summer with the Raptors. He now has the Clippers \u2014 abysmal for much of their existence \u2013 looking like a championship favorite for 2019-20. \u201cWhen I moved into my current house,\u201d says Jacquelyne Leonard, \u201cI was unpacking and found an old Bible. I opened it and Mark had a prayer in it. He had made a list of things he wanted to happen in his life, as I asked him to do. One said, `Watch my boy go to the pros.\u2019 If Mark was sitting here right now, he\u2019d say, `I told y\u2019all.\u2019 Unfortunately he\u2019s not around to see this.\u201d * * * The car wash once run by Mark Leonard has twice changed hands and operates today as HB Tires and Wheels . Business is brisk because this is a car city. The signage is different. The old employees are long gone and rusty cars fill the lot. There are, however, three holes near the bottom of the facade, right by the front door, which the manager says were made by bullets. If only walls could talk. He says every once in a while, an old customer will mention the shooting and excitedly ask him if he knew whose dad it was, and the manager nods respectfully before Kawhi Leonard\u2019s name is mentioned. Jacquelyne Leonard kept the business open after the murder, but that spring she was shot in a drive-by from a truck , almost in the exact same spot in the parking lot. That, too, became an unresolved case, and detectives aren\u2019t sure if the shootings were related. She said she nearly lost her legs: \u201cThe doctors told me they were going to amputate, they were so damaged. I had eight surgeries just to help me walk again.\u201d She was also three months pregnant, but soon delivered Mark Leonard\u2019s last child, and some of Mark\u2019s old high school football teammates and employees helped raise the boy. Today, a decade later, mother and son are healthy and happy, she reports. Zion Mark Anthony Leonard is 11 and plays basketball. Not as reserved as his famous half-brother, he is asking his mother what happened to his father. Three months ago Kawhi Leonard held his Clippers\u2019 jersey for the first time, at a team news conference where they formally introduced him and Paul George, another star making a return to Los Angeles-area roots. True to his nature, Leonard was mostly reserved at the ceremony, even on a day made for enthusiasm. Seizing the chance to crown themselves a team for all of Los Angeles, the Clippers held the event at Green Meadows Recreation Center in South L.A., their way of giving light to a community that rarely if ever sees rich and famous athletes. It was perhaps only a coincidence that, just a few stoplights away, on the other side of the 105 Freeway, on a lot that once was a car wash, is where Leonard first learned the value of hard work. Perhaps soon, he\u2019ll learn who stole the life of the man who taught him that. * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. "},{"id":31066,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/guards-russell-westbrook-chris-paul-face-former-teams","date":"2019-10-29","title":"Russell Westbrook steals spotlight as Rockets spoil Chris Paul's return to Houston","content":" HOUSTON \u2014 Russell Westbrook scrapping under the rim for a loose ball with good friend Steven Adams set the tone for odd visuals Monday in a clash between star point guards facing their former teams. Oklahoma City point guard Chris Paul returned to Houston for the first time since the Rockets moved him for first-round picks and pick swaps over the summer to acquire Westbrook , who dominated the night of reunions by nearly logging his second consecutive triple-double (21 points, 12 rebounds, 9 assists) to fuel a 116-112 triumph . In doing so, Westbrook nearly became the first player to post triple-doubles against all 30 NBA teams. \u201cThis is how it goes,\u201d Westbrook said. \u201cWhen I hoop, I have no friends. On the court, they know not to talk to me. Steven\u2019s a real close friend of mine. But inside those lines, there\u2019s no friends. Spalding, that\u2019s my friend, and my teammates. That\u2019s it. If you try to be my friend, I ain\u2019t gonna say [expletive] to you.\u201d Shortly after saying those words, Westbrook walked down the hall to the Thunder locker room, where he hugged coach Billy Donovan before entering as his former teammates dressed. Westbrook played 11 seasons with the Thunder before the July trade, and earned NBA All-Star recognition on eight occasions in addition to capturing the 2017 Kia MVP. \u201cHe obviously has done an enormous amount for the organization, for the state and the city,\u201d Donovan said. \u201cI\u2019ve always respected how hard he competed and played. We had a chance to spend four great years together. It was good to just connect.\u201d As Westbrook strolled into the locker room, several Thunder officials approached him for hugs. Glass of water in hand, the point guard eventually settled near Adams\u2019 locker adjacent to injured guard Andre Roberson. Nearby, Paul dressed and joked that Westbrook could be fined by the league for entering the opponent\u2019s locker room, which drew laughter from all over the room. Westbrook eventually moved to Paul\u2019s locker, where the two talked quietly for several minutes. On the floor, though, Westbrook overcame a slow start to dominate over the final three quarters which helped push the Rockets to their second consecutive victory. Westbrook finished at a game-best plus-19, while James Harden led all scoring with 40 points. Westbrook has posted a 20-point double-double in all three of Houston\u2019s games this season, including a triple-double Saturday in a win over the New Orleans Pelicans. Westbrook has also pulled down 38 rebounds over his first three games, which ranks as the most by a Rocket through the first three games of the season since Dwight Howard registered 51 rebounds during the 2013-14 season. In addition, Westbrook moved into 20th on the NBA\u2019s all-time assists list (6,918). \u201cHe just brings a different dynamic to the game: his speed, his pace, his athleticism, his playmaking ability,\u201d Harden said. \u201cHe does so much and creates for his teammates. It\u2019s pretty tough to guard. He\u2019s a superstar. But he\u2019s getting offensive rebounds, he\u2019s hustling. He\u2019s doing the dirty things that help you win. It feels good to have that on your side.\u201d On the other side, Paul didn\u2019t fare as well against his former team, finishing with 15 points and four assists. Paul missed his first five shots, making his first bucket with 54.9 seconds left in the first half. I\u2019ll forever be grateful for that.\u201d Paul played two seasons in Houston (2017-19), averaging 17.1 points, 8.0 assists and 5 rebounds, before the club traded him to Oklahoma City. With the Rockets leading that series 3-2, Paul suffered a hamstring injury that forced him out of the last two games. \u201cHe\u2019s one of the best point guards that\u2019s ever played and still is. Then we give it an overall grade on a scale of 1-5 Robert Horrys, named for the patron saint of last-second answered prayers. * * * The Ja Morant \u2013 Kyrie Irving duel dominated most of the night. But when the young Grizzlies needed to calm down and come up with their first win of the season, they turned to one of the few veterans on their roster as the final moments of overtime ticked away. Morant used as much of the remaining 3.7 seconds as he dared to advance the ball before shoveling a pass to Jae Crowder, who drilled the straightaway 3-pointer for Memphis\u2019 134-133 win over the Nets. * * * DIFFICULTY: Morant did all the table-setting, speeding downcourt and drawing two defenders to him like a magnet. That allowed Crowder to receive a simple shovel pass with ample space to shoot north to south, a beeline look the veteran coolly hit as time expired. GAME SITUATION: It looked as though Brooklyn\u2019s Joe Harris was going to wind up the hero on the previous possession. His unlikely high-flying tip-in put Brooklyn up 133-131 with just 3.7 seconds left in overtime. Between that, Ja Morant\u2019s turnover on the previous possession and the fact that Crowder had not scored at all until overtime, the game\u2019s momentum was not on Memphis\u2019 side heading into the final possession. CELEBRATION: For a young Grizzlies team seeking to establish an identity, a veteran like Crowder draws immediate credibility and respect. Some of his younger teammates had already started sprinting toward him before the ball hit bottom, and the entire team had run him down by the time Crowder was pounding his chest in triumph. GRADE: An impressive and potentially foundational win for a rebuilding Grizzlies squad. The Mavericks\u2019 leading scorer went off for 34 points the game prior, the most in a season opener by a player under 21 years old in NBA history . Doncic drilled a high-arching dagger against the Pelicans. Young drained a rainbow clincher against the Magic. The Hawks drafted Doncic with the No. 3 pick in 2018, but traded away his rights to the Mavericks in exchange for Young and a 2019 Draft pick (Cam Reddish, who looks great on defense but has struggled offensively to begin the season). During the 2018-19 season, both players ended up battling for the Kia Rookie of the Year award, with Doncic emerging as the winner. Doncic reacted to Young\u2019s game-winner on Twitter, and the two often laud each other\u2019s highlights on Instagram. There\u2019s no battle for Rookie of the Year anymore. Young is already the undeniable leader of a young team in the foundational stage of their process. He\u2019s in complete command of what Hawks coach Lloyd Pierce wants done, while still needing to smooth out the rough edges of his game as he continues to mature physically. Young\u2019s belief in his own abilities and what he can do on the floor, however, shines through in the way he plays. (Two games into this season he\u2019s averaging 38.5 points and shooting 58 percent from the floor and 55 percent from beyond the 3-point line to go along with nine rebounds and seven assists). And those are mistakes you shouldn\u2019t make.\u201d Fultz, of course, is still working on that part of his game. Clifford\u2019s decision to go with him, instead of starter D.J. Augustin or former Rookie of the Year Michael Carter-Williams, speaks volumes about the confidence being placed in Fultz this season. And if what he\u2019s shown early on, both in training camp and the preseason as well as the Magic\u2019s first two games, is any indication, those flashes, those bursts of the breathtaking play he\u2019s capable of might stretch into something much more significant. \u201cIt shows the trust and it shows the work I put in,\u201d Fultz said of Clifford\u2019s decision to go with him for those final four, crunch-time minutes. \u201cAnd for me, it\u2019s learning experiences. Every time I can step on the floor and learn and just be the best player I can be. And down the stretch, that\u2019s one of the best times to be on the court, when all the pressure\u2019s on you.
